				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Target Corp.">Target Corp.</a>)</span></div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the defunct Canadian subsidiary, see <a href="/wiki/Target_Canada" title="Target Canada">Target Canada</a>. For the unrelated Australian company owned by Wesfarmers, see <a href="/wiki/Target_Australia" title="Target Australia">Target Australia</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<p><b>Target Corporation</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retail</a> corporation. It is the 8th-largest retailer in the United States, and is a component of the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500_Index" title="S&amp;P 500 Index">S&amp;P 500 Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> It is unrelated to <a href="/wiki/Target_Australia" title="Target Australia">Target Australia</a>.

src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> US$11.297 billion</li><li><span style="font-size:85%;">(FY 2019)</span></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist nowrap"><ul><li>~360,000</li><li><span style="font-size:85%;">(FY 2019)</span></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">Target Brands, Inc.<br>Target Capital Corporation<br>Target Enterprise, Inc.<br>Target General Merchandise, Inc.<br><a href="/wiki/Shipt" title="Shipt">Shipt</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist nowrap"><ul><li><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://target.com">Target.com</a></span></li><li><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://corporate.target.com/">Corporate.Target.com</a></span></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-10KFEB32018_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10KFEB32018-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Target established itself as the day time division of the Dayton-Hudson Corporation in the 1970s; it began expanding the store nationwide in the 1980s and introduced new store formats under the Target brand in the 1990s. The company has found success as a cheap-chic player in the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">[5]</a></sup> The parent company was renamed the Target Corporation in 2000 and divested itself of its last department store chains in 2004. It suffered from a massive and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Target_Corporation#2013_security_breach" title="History of Target Corporation">highly publicized security breach of customer credit card data</a> and the failure of its short-lived <a href="/wiki/Target_Canada" title="Target Canada">Target Canada</a> subsidiary in the early 2010s but experienced revitalized success with its expansion in urban markets within the United States. As of February 2nd, 2019, Target operates 1,844<sup id="cite_ref-10KFEB32018_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10KFEB32018-2">[2]</a></sup> stores throughout the United States. The company is ranked No. 39 on 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500"><i>Fortune</i> 500</a> list of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Their retail formats include the <a href="/wiki/Discount_store" title="Discount store">discount store</a> Target, the hypermarket SuperTarget, and "small-format" stores previously named CityTarget and TargetExpress before being consolidated under the Target branding. Target is often recognized for its emphasis on "the needs of its younger, image-conscious shoppers", whereas its rival Walmart more heavily relies on its strategy of "always low prices".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Store_formats">Store formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Store formats" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Target">Target</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Target" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_Rock_Hill,_SC_(7151362297).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Target_Rock_Hill%2C_SC_%287151362297%29.jpg/200px-Target_Rock_Hill%2C_SC_%287151362297%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 150px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Target_Rock_Hill%2C_SC_%287151362297%29.jpg/200px-Target_Rock_Hill%2C_SC_%287151362297%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="150" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_Rock_Hill,_SC_(7151362297).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The exterior of a typical Target store in <a href="/wiki/Rock_Hill,_South_Carolina" title="Rock Hill, South Carolina">Rock Hill, South Carolina</a>, in May 2012</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CVSTarget19.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/CVSTarget19.jpg/200px-CVSTarget19.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="176" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2946" data-file-height="2587"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 176px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/CVSTarget19.jpg/200px-CVSTarget19.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="176" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CVSTarget19.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CVS_Pharmacy" title="CVS Pharmacy">CVS Pharmacy</a> inside of a Target store.</div></div></div>
<p>The first <b>Target</b> <a href="/wiki/Discount_store" title="Discount store">discount store</a> opened in <a href="/wiki/Roseville,_Minnesota" title="Roseville, Minnesota">Roseville, Minnesota</a> on May 1, 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-TargetThroughTheYears_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TargetThroughTheYears-9">[9]</a></sup> Present-day properties are roughly 135,000 square feet (12,500 m<sup>2</sup>) and sell general merchandise including <a href="/wiki/Category:Hardlines_(retail)" title="Category:Hardlines (retail)">hardlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Softlines_(retail)" title="Category:Softlines (retail)">softlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UrbanShoppers_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UrbanShoppers-10">[10]</a></sup> While many Target stores follow a standard <a href="/wiki/Big-box_store" title="Big-box store">big-box</a> architectural style,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> the company has focused on "customizing each new store to ensure a locally-relevant experience [...] that best fit the surrounding neighborhood’s needs" since August 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Initially, only SuperTarget locations operated <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks Coffee</a> counters, although they were integrated into general merchandise stores through their expanded partnership beginning in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p><p>Target introduced the "PFresh" store prototype in 2006, which expanded its grocery selection in general merchandise locations by an upwards of 200-percent. Newly constructed stores that follow the PFresh format are roughly 1,500 square feet (140 m<sup>2</sup>) larger than properties without groceries, although retain the Target branding because their offerings are considerably more limited than SuperTarget. The company remodeled 109 stores accordingly in 2006 and renovated another 350 stores the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The company's decision to close their garden centers opened floor space for PFresh expansion and larger seasonal departments beginning in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>On June 15, 2015 <a href="/wiki/CVS_Health" title="CVS Health">CVS Health</a> announced an agreement with Target to acquire all of Target's pharmacies and clinic businesses for around $1.9 billion. The Target pharmacies were rebranded as CVS Health pharmacies which totaled 1,672 pharmacies. The Target clinics were also rebranded as MinuteClinic. The acquisition of the Target pharmacies enabled CVS to expand its market into Seattle, Denver, Portland, and Salt Lake City. The Target pharmacies were rebranded to CVS Health pharmacies in February 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bi-2016feb03_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bi-2016feb03-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="SuperTarget">SuperTarget</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: SuperTarget" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SuperTarget_.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/SuperTarget_.jpg/200px-SuperTarget_.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 150px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/SuperTarget_.jpg/200px-SuperTarget_.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="150" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SuperTarget_.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The exterior of a SuperTarget in <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a>, in October 2005</div></div></div>
<p>The first <b>Target Greatland</b> location opened in <a href="/wiki/Apple_Valley,_Minnesota" title="Apple Valley, Minnesota">Apple Valley, Minnesota</a> in September 1990. They were about fifty-percent larger than traditional Target stores, and pioneered company standards including an increased number of checkout lanes and price scanners, larger aisles, expanded pharmacy and photography departments, and a food court. Target Greatland locations have since been converted to stores following the PFresh format beginning in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p><p>The first <b>Super Target</b> <a href="/wiki/Hypermarket" title="Hypermarket">hypermarket</a> opened in <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a> in 1995, and expanded upon the Target Greatland concept with the inclusion of a full grocery department.<sup id="cite_ref-TargetThroughTheYears_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TargetThroughTheYears-9">[9]</a></sup> The company expanded their grocery assortment in 2003 and adopted the modified tagline "Eat Well. Pay Less." (in reference to their tagline "Expect More. Pay Less.") in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-TargetThroughTheYears_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TargetThroughTheYears-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReboundRecipe_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReboundRecipe-19">[19]</a></sup> In the early 2000s, 43 locations (of nearly 100) featured <a href="/wiki/E-Trade" title="E-Trade">E-Trade</a> trading stations, although they were all closed by June 2003 after E-Trade determined that "we were not able to make it into a profitable distribution channel."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p><p>When comparing itself with rival Walmart Supercenter hypermarkets, then-chief executive Gregg Steinhafel opined that <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> operates like "a grocer that happens to also sell general merchandise," where in contrast its less aggressive expansion of SuperTarget stores is indicative of their position that the grocery industry as a "high-impact, low-cost" side project.<sup id="cite_ref-ReboundRecipe_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReboundRecipe-19">[19]</a></sup> The company operated 239 SuperTarget locations as of September 2015;<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> they each encompass an estimate of 174,000 square feet (16,200 m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2015, Target made the announcement of "Big or small, our stores have one thing in common: they're all Target."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Since then newer stores have opened under the Target name. Existing SuperTarget stores retained the name on the buildings although some have become Target through remodels.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Small-format_Target">Small-format Target</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Small-format Target" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_Boston_Fenway_(MA).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Target_Boston_Fenway_%28MA%29.jpg/200px-Target_Boston_Fenway_%28MA%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 150px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Target_Boston_Fenway_%28MA%29.jpg/200px-Target_Boston_Fenway_%28MA%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="150" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_Boston_Fenway_(MA).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The exterior of the CityTarget in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, in October 2015, now re-branded as Target</div></div></div>
<p>While typical Target locations are approximately 135,000 square feet (12,500 m<sup>2</sup>), the majority of "small-format" <b>CityTarget</b> stores are roughly 80,000 square feet (7,400 m<sup>2</sup>). The first stores were opened in July 2012, in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-UrbanShoppers_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UrbanShoppers-10">[10]</a></sup> the 160,000 square feet (15,000 m<sup>2</sup>) location in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> is the largest CityTarget and opened in July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-24">[24]</a></sup> <b>TargetExpress</b> stores hover around 14,000 square feet (1,300 m<sup>2</sup>) to 21,000 square feet (2,000 m<sup>2</sup>); the first opened in <a href="/wiki/Dinkytown" title="Dinkytown">Dinkytown</a> near the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota" title="University of Minnesota">University of Minnesota</a> in July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Products in these flexible format properties are typically sold in smaller packages geared towards customers using <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transportation</a>. Locations built in college communities often carry an extended home department of apartment and dormitory furnishings.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In August 2015, Target announced that it would rename its nine CityTarget and five TargetExpress stores as Target beginning that October, deciding that "Big or small, our stores have one thing in common: they're all Target."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-24">[24]</a></sup> The first small-format stores under the unified naming scheme opened later that month in Chicago, <a href="/wiki/Rosslyn,_Arlington,_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosslyn, Arlington, Virginia">Rosslyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The company opened a 45,000 square foot store in the <a href="/wiki/Tribeca" title="Tribeca">Tribeca</a> neighborhood of New York in October 2016. In that same month, three other similar-sized stores opened in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cupertino,_California" title="Cupertino, California">Cupertino, California</a>, and the area around <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_University" title="Pennsylvania State University">Pennsylvania State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">[5]</a></sup> There is also a downtown Target in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>.
</p><p>Nearly all of its planned openings through 2019 are small formats, which is less than 50,000 square feet.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">[5]</a></sup> The goal of these smaller format stores is to win over the business of millennial customers. The nearly 30 new locations will be situated in college towns or densely populated areas.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Brands_and_subsidiaries">Brands and subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Brands and subsidiaries" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>As of 2018 Target has four subsidiaries: <a href="/wiki/Target_Brands,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Target Brands, Inc.">Target Brands, Inc.</a>, Target Capital Corporation, Target Enterprise, Inc. and Target General Merchandise, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TargetCanada.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/TargetCanada.JPG/220px-TargetCanada.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 146px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/TargetCanada.JPG/220px-TargetCanada.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="146" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TargetCanada.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Target cash registers.</div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_and_Retail_Services">Financial and Retail Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Financial and Retail Services" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Financial and Retail Services (FRS), formerly Target Financial Services (TFS), issues Target's credit cards, known as the Target REDcard (formerly the Target Guest Card), issued through Target National Bank (formerly Retailers National Bank) for consumers and through Target Bank for businesses. Target Financial Services also oversees GiftCard balances. Target launched its <a href="/wiki/Personal_identification_number" title="Personal identification number">PIN</a>-x debit card, the Target Check Card, which was later re-branded the Target Debit Card. The Target Debit Card withdraws funds from the customer's existing checking account, and allows for up to $40 "cash back". The debit card allows guests to save five percent off each purchase. In late 2017, Target replaced its REDcard slogan "Save 5% Today, Tomorrow, &amp; Everyday with Target REDcard" when it rolled out new benefits for REDcard holders by offering exclusive products on Target.com and preorders with "Everyday Savings. Exclusive Extras."<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Target_Sourcing_Services">Target Sourcing Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Target Sourcing Services" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>This global sourcing organization locates merchandise from around the world for Target and helps import the merchandise to the United States. Such merchandise includes garments, furniture, bedding, and towels. TSS has 27 full-service offices, 48 quality-control offices, and seven concessionaires located throughout the world. TSS employs 1,200 people. Its engineers are responsible for evaluating the factories that do business with Target Corporation for quality, as well as labor rights and transshipment issues.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> TSS was acquired by Target Corporation in 1998, was founded in 1916 as the Associated Merchandising Corporation, and was previously owned by the clients it served.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Target Sourcing Services ceased operations in its department store group, the division of the former Associated Merchandising Corporation that acted as a buying office for <a href="/wiki/Saks,_Inc." title="Saks, Inc.">Saks, Inc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bloomingdale%27s" title="Bloomingdale's">Bloomingdale's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stage_Stores_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Stage Stores Inc.">Stage Stores Inc.</a>, <a href="/wiki/T.J.Maxx" class="mw-redirect" title="T.J.Maxx">T.J.Maxx</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marshalls" title="Marshalls">Marshalls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-amc_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amc-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_label_brands">Private label brands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Private label brands" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Target,_Dublin,_CA_5_2017-01-13.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Target%2C_Dublin%2C_CA_5_2017-01-13.jpg/220px-Target%2C_Dublin%2C_CA_5_2017-01-13.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Target%2C_Dublin%2C_CA_5_2017-01-13.jpg/220px-Target%2C_Dublin%2C_CA_5_2017-01-13.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Target,_Dublin,_CA_5_2017-01-13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Target electronics department.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Target,_Dublin,_CA_17_2017-05-10.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Target%2C_Dublin%2C_CA_17_2017-05-10.jpg/220px-Target%2C_Dublin%2C_CA_17_2017-05-10.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="4032"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Target%2C_Dublin%2C_CA_17_2017-05-10.jpg/220px-Target%2C_Dublin%2C_CA_17_2017-05-10.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Target,_Dublin,_CA_17_2017-05-10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Target grocery department.</div></div></div>
<p>Target Brands is the company's brand management division that oversees the company's <a href="/wiki/Private_label" title="Private label">private label</a> products. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Bullseye_(mascot)" title="Bullseye (mascot)">Bullseye</a> Dog is a mascot, and the Bullseye Design and 'Target' are registered trademarks of Target Brands.
</p>
<ul><li><b>Good &amp; Gather</b>, food and beverage brand replacing Archer Farms and Simply Balanced.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Archer Farms</b>, up-market grocery products;</li>
<li><b>Market Pantry</b>, value grocery products;</li>
<li><b>Simply Balanced</b>, organic grocery products;</li>
<li><b>Sutton &amp; Dodge</b>, a premium meat line;</li>
<li><b>Boots &amp; Barkley</b>, a pet food and supply line;</li>
<li><b>Embark</b>, an outdoor gear line of camping and travel equipment;</li>
<li><b>Room Essentials</b>, a low-end home goods line.</li>
<li><b>Threshold</b>, a premium furniture line;</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Cannon_Mills" title="Cannon Mills">Fieldcrest</a></b>, bedding &amp; bath line in partnership with brand owner <a href="/wiki/Iconix_Brand_Group" title="Iconix Brand Group">Iconix Brand Group</a>;</li>
<li><b>up &amp; up</b>. Target issued a re-launch of the Target brand as <b>up&amp;up</b> to include an expanded product selection and a new design. The <b>up &amp; up</b> brand offers essential commodities including household, healthcare, beauty, baby, and personal care products. The brand claims to offer products of equal quality to national brands at a fraction of the cost, averaging a savings of 30 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> As of September 2009, up &amp; up offers over 800 products across 40 categories.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></li></ul><p>Other private labels include brands launched in July 2016, during Back to School sales.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TargetINCLTHS.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/TargetINCLTHS.jpg/220px-TargetINCLTHS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/TargetINCLTHS.jpg/220px-TargetINCLTHS.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TargetINCLTHS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Goodfellow &amp; Co. clothes at a Target store.</div></div></div>
<ul><li><b>Pillowfort</b>, a children's line of bedding</li>
<li><b>Cat and Jack</b>, a children's line of apparel and accessories.</li>
<li><b>Cloud Island</b>, a baby's line of bedding and clothing.</li>
<li><b>Project 62</b>, a household goods line placed alongside Room Essentials.</li>
<li><b>Goodfellow &amp; Co.</b>, a clothing and personal-care line for men, with the name being an homage to their beginnings as <b>Goodfellow Dry Goods</b></li>
<li><b>A New Day</b>, a clothing line for women.</li>
<li><b>JoyLab</b>, a fitness clothing line.</li>
<li><b>Hearth and Hand</b>, a home &amp; lifestyle brand, in collaboration with Magnolia</li></ul><p>After the launch, the clothing and bedding brands made a big hit and was successful. Target executives claim that the new brands increased sales by $1 billion and increased 15% in revenue, only during their first year.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p><p>8 Target private label brands that launched in 2018<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><b>Universal Thread</b>, a denim lifestyle brand</li>
<li><b>Opalhouse</b>, eclectic home decor</li>
<li><b>Heyday</b>, a line electronic accessories</li>
<li><b>Original Use</b>, male clothing brand targeting Gen-Z and Millennials.</li>
<li><b>Wild Fable</b>, women's clothing brand targeting Gen-Z.</li>
<li><b>Made By Design</b>, a homelines brand, made up of home basics like towels, cooking utensils, glassware, plates, pots, kitchen gadgets, and more.</li>
<li><b>Prologue</b>, sophisticated female line of clothing.</li>
<li><b>Smartly</b>, essential commodity brand including household, healthcare, beauty, and personal care products.</li></ul><p>In addition, Target recently released 3 new intimates, loungewear, and sleepwear brands for women on February 25, 2019:<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><b>Auden</b>, an intimates and lingerie exclusive brand</li>
<li><b>Stars Above</b>, their in-house brand for sleepwear</li>
<li><b>Colsie</b>, an intimates and loungewear brand</li></ul><p>On January 9, 2020, Target announced its new activewear brand, <b>All In Motion</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>Former brands include:
</p>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Cherokee_Inc." title="Cherokee Inc.">Cherokee</a></b>, children's and women's clothing. On September 10, 2015, it was announced that Target stores would cease carrying the brand when its partnership with <a href="/wiki/Cherokee_Inc." title="Cherokee Inc.">Cherokee Inc.</a> expired on January 31, 2017. It was replaced by Cat &amp; Jack;</li>
<li><b>Circo</b>,  toddler's and kids clothing. The brand was replaced by Cat &amp; Jack upon debut.</li>
<li><b>Merona</b>, a clothing brand purchased by Target in 1991;</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Mossimo" title="Mossimo">Mossimo Supply Co.</a></b>, a clothing line. In partnership with the brand owner <a href="/wiki/Iconix_Brand_Group" title="Iconix Brand Group">Iconix Brand Group</a>;</li>
<li><b>Xhilaration</b> and <b>Gilligan &amp; O'Malley</b> product lines of intimates and sleepwear were discontinued after the release of the brands Auden, Stars Above, and Colsie.</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Website">Website</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Website" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>

data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Increase_Negative.svg/17px-Increase_Negative.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Increase_Negative.svg/22px-Increase_Negative.svg.png 2x"> </span> 344 global, <noscript><img alt="Negative increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Increase_Negative.svg/11px-Increase_Negative.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Negative increase" width="11" height="11" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 11px;height: 11px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Increase_Negative.svg/11px-Increase_Negative.svg.png" data-alt="Negative increase" data-width="11" data-height="11" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Increase_Negative.svg/17px-Increase_Negative.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Increase_Negative.svg/22px-Increase_Negative.svg.png 2x"> </span> 98 in the United States (October 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-alexa_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexa-39">[39]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Commercial</th><td>Yes</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Registration</th><td>Optional but required for some features</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Launched</th><td>2000, August 2011<span class="noprint">; 8 years ago</span><span style="display:none"> (<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2011-08</span>)</span> (rebrand)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Current status</th><td class="category">Online</td></tr></tbody></table><p>Target.com owns and oversees the company's <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a> initiatives, such as the Target.com domain. Founded in early 2000 as target.direct, it was formed by separating the company's existing e-commerce operations from its retailing division and combining it with its Rivertown Trading direct marketing unit into a stand-alone subsidiary.<sup id="cite_ref-namechange_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-namechange-40">[40]</a></sup> In 2002, target.direct and <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a>'s subsidiary Amazon Enterprise Solutions created a partnership in which Amazon.com would provide order fulfillment and guest services for Target.com in exchange for fixed and variable fees. After the company sold Marshall Field's and Mervyn's in 2004, target.direct became Target.com. The domain <i>target.com</i> attracted at least 288 million visitors annually by 2008, according to a <a href="/wiki/Compete.com" title="Compete.com">Compete.com</a> survey.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In August 2009, Target announced that they would build and manage a new Target.com platform, independent of Amazon.com. This new platform was to launch in 2011, in advance of the holiday season. Prior to the announcement, Target and Amazon had extended their partnership until 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In January 2010, Target announced their vendor partners for the re-platforming project. These partners include <a href="/wiki/Sapient_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Sapient Corporation">Sapient</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endeca" title="Endeca">Endeca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autonomy_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomy Corporation">Autonomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Commerce" title="Sterling Commerce">Sterling Commerce</a> and <a href="/wiki/HUGE_(digital_agency)" class="mw-redirect" title="HUGE (digital agency)">Huge</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The re-platformed Target.com officially launched on August 23, 2011, effectively ending the partnership with Amazon.com.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_subsidiaries">Former subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Former subsidiaries" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>Target Portrait Studio</b> was a chain of <a href="/wiki/Portrait_photography" title="Portrait photography">portrait studios</a> that were located in select Target stores. The chain, which was operated by <a href="/wiki/Lifetouch" title="Lifetouch">Lifetouch</a>, opened in 1996 and ceased operations on January 28, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Target Canada</b> were the chain of Target stores in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. It was formed in 2013 when Target acquired <a href="/wiki/Zellers" title="Zellers">Zellers</a> and converted into Target stores. Target Canada was in operation for two years until the closure of all stores in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Supply_chain">Supply chain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Supply chain" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Targetsemitruck.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Targetsemitruck.jpg/250px-Targetsemitruck.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="196" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2743" data-file-height="2147"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 250px;height: 196px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Targetsemitruck.jpg/250px-Targetsemitruck.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="250" data-height="196" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Targetsemitruck.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Truck arriving at a Target distribution center.</div></div></div>
<p>As of May 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Target Corporation operates 39 distribution centers across the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> With the exception of vendor supplied items, such as greeting cards and soda, these distribution centers ship items directly to Target stores. Also, unlike <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a>, Target's grocery selection does not come from their own distribution centers, but from the companies with whom Target has partnered.<sup id="cite_ref-rowley_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowley-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>The retail chain's first distribution center opened in <a href="/wiki/Fridley,_Minnesota" title="Fridley, Minnesota">Fridley, Minnesota</a>, in 1969. It included a computerized distribution system and was known as the Northern Distribution Center. During this time, the chain consisted of seventeen stores after having expanded into <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> and Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-growth_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-growth-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>On August 9, 2004, Target announced to their suppliers that they were going to perform a trial on the effects of <a href="/wiki/Radio-frequency_identification" title="Radio-frequency identification">radio-frequency identification</a> on the efficiency of <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">supply chain management</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex</a>. This trial involved one Target distribution center and ten nearby Target stores. Here, RFID tags were placed on the bar codes of pallets and cartons to track the goods from the suppliers to the distribution center, and from the distribution center to the stores.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> As of 2009, RFID had been phased out of the Dallas–Fort Worth stores.
</p><p>Target opened three new distribution centers in 2006 (<a href="/wiki/Rialto,_California" title="Rialto, California">Rialto, California</a>, <a href="/wiki/DeKalb,_Illinois" title="DeKalb, Illinois">DeKalb, Illinois</a>) and one in 2009 (<a href="/wiki/Newton,_North_Carolina" title="Newton, North Carolina">Newton, North Carolina</a>) to support the growth of its stores. On January 27, 2009, Target announced the closing of its distribution center in <a href="/wiki/Maumelle,_Arkansas" title="Maumelle, Arkansas">Maumelle, Arkansas</a>, the second-oldest in the company. The reason cited was the need to ensure that Target remains competitive in the long-term.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In June 2009 Target opened a new distribution center to supply more than 60 stores in three states.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>SuperTarget and PFresh stores require fresh produce, refrigerated and frozen items. Food distribution centers owned by <a href="/wiki/SuperValu_(United_States)" title="SuperValu (United States)">SuperValu</a> have been utilized by Target for many years. In October 2003, SuperValu's facility in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>, was converted to serve Target exclusively.<sup id="cite_ref-RT_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT-53">[53]</a></sup> The same change was implemented at the SuperValu center in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth, Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TARGET_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TARGET-54">[54]</a></sup> A new distribution center was constructed by Target in <a href="/wiki/Lake_City,_Florida" title="Lake City, Florida">Lake City, Florida</a>, to serve the Southeast, but it was operated by SuperValu until 2011 when it transitioned to Target.<sup id="cite_ref-RT_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT-53">[53]</a></sup> A fourth center in <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Falls,_Iowa" title="Cedar Falls, Iowa">Cedar Falls, Iowa</a>, opened in 2009 and is unique in that it is located adjacent to a standard Target Distribution Center, each utilizing the same dispatch office.<sup id="cite_ref-TARGET_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TARGET-54">[54]</a></sup> Other warehouses owned by SuperValu are still used in other regions, but Target plans to replace those over the next few years.<sup id="cite_ref-RT_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT-53">[53]</a></sup> In Colorado, stores are serviced through <i>FreshPack Produce Inc.</i> of <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rowley_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowley-48">[48]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Mid-Atlantic region">mid-Atlantic region</a>/<a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> market, <a href="/wiki/C%26S_Wholesale_Grocers" title="C&amp;S Wholesale Grocers">C&amp;S Wholesale Grocers</a> services the fresh produce, meat, dairy, bakery, &amp; frozen needs to "PFresh" stores. Target partnered with <a href="/wiki/Swisslog_Holding" title="Swisslog Holding">Swisslog Holding</a> to use a semi-automated monorail picking system called the CaddyPick system for use in the food distribution centers.
</p><p>The company operates four facilities to receive shipments from overseas manufacturers and suppliers. They are located near ports at <a href="/wiki/Rialto,_California" title="Rialto, California">Rialto, California</a>; <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah, Georgia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Lacey,_Washington" title="Lacey, Washington">Lacey, Washington</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">Suffolk, Virginia</a>. Merchandise received is sent directly to Regional Distribution Centers. Internet sales orders from the Target Direct division, which operates from the Target.com website, are processed by the facility in <a href="/wiki/Woodbury,_Minnesota" title="Woodbury, Minnesota">Woodbury, Minnesota</a>, with some support from <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah, Georgia</a>, and other vendors. New centers opened in <a href="/wiki/Ontario,_California" title="Ontario, California">Ontario, California</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona" title="Tucson, Arizona">Tucson, Arizona</a>, in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-TARGET_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TARGET-54">[54]</a></sup></p>

</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Headquarters" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_Plaza_South.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Target_Plaza_South.jpg/220px-Target_Plaza_South.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="297" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="487" data-file-height="657"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 297px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Target_Plaza_South.jpg/220px-Target_Plaza_South.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="297" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_Plaza_South.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Target_Plaza_South" title="Target Plaza South">Target Plaza South</a>, a portion of the Target Corporation headquarters complex in downtown <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis, United States">Minneapolis, United States</a>; the building originally featured the Target Light System, created by using <a href="/wiki/3M" title="3M">3M</a> light pipes<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> but was replaced by more energy-efficient LEDs in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Target Corporation has its headquarters on <a href="/wiki/Nicollet_Mall" title="Nicollet Mall">Nicollet Mall</a> in Minneapolis,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> near the site of the original Goodfellows store.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The complex includes Target Plaza North and <a href="/wiki/Target_Plaza_South" title="Target Plaza South">Target Plaza South</a>. Ryan Companies developed the complex, and Ellerbe Becket served as the architect. Target had the approximately $260 million complex developed to provide one location of office space for 6,000 employees. The 14-story Target Plaza North has 600,000 square feet (56,000 m<sup>2</sup>) of office and retail space while the 32-story Target Plaza South has 1,250,000 square feet (116,000 m<sup>2</sup>) of space.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>Brian Cornell is the CEO of Target Corporation. In January 2016, Cornell began making home visits in an effort to understand better the needs and desires of his customers.<sup id="cite_ref-Target_CEO_Brian_Cornell_visiting_homes_of_customers_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Target_CEO_Brian_Cornell_visiting_homes_of_customers-59">[59]</a></sup> In January 2016, Target fired Tina Tyler from her job as chief stores officer. She was replaced with long-time employee Janna Potts.<sup id="cite_ref-Wall_Street_Journal:_Home_Depot_Replaces_Head_of_U.S._Stores_Business_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wall_Street_Journal:_Home_Depot_Replaces_Head_of_U.S._Stores_Business-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Diversity">Diversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Diversity" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company states that "individuality may include a wide spectrum of attributes such as personal style, age, race, gender, ethnicity, sexual orientation, language, physical ability, religion, family, citizenship status, socio-economic circumstances, education, and life experiences."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p><p>The Target employee diversity initiative is called "All Together Target".<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> It specifically seeks to work with vendors and contractors that are owned by minorities or women.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2012, the company extended the team member discount to same-sex partners of employees. It had received a 100 on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign" title="Human Rights Campaign">Human Rights Campaign</a> Corporate Equality Index Score, prior to donating funds to <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Forward" title="Minnesota Forward">Minnesota Forward</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Colored_People" class="mw-redirect" title="National Association for the Advancement of Colored People">National Association for the Advancement of Colored People</a> has repeatedly given Target failing grades on its annual Economic Reciprocity Initiative report card, a measure of the company's "commitment to the African-American citizenry". In 2003 and 2005, the NAACP has rated Target an "F" on this report; in 2004, Target was rated a "D-".<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In 2006, when Target was asked why it didn't participate in the survey again,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> a representative explained, "Target views diversity as being inclusive of all people from all different backgrounds, not just <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">one group</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2006, the <a href="/wiki/National_Federation_of_the_Blind" title="National Federation of the Blind">National Federation of the Blind</a> (NFB) filed a <a href="/wiki/National_Federation_of_the_Blind_v._Target_Corp." title="National Federation of the Blind v. Target Corp.">class action discrimination lawsuit</a> in Northern California's Alameda County Superior Court, claiming that Target's commercial website contains "thousands of access barriers that make it difficult, if not impossible, for blind customers to use."<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Target Corporation settled the lawsuit in October 2008, paying $6 million and agreeing to work with the NFB over the next three years improving the usability of the Target.com site.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>
August 24, 2009, the United States <a href="/wiki/Equal_Employment_Opportunity_Commission" title="Equal Employment Opportunity Commission">Equal Employment Opportunity Commission</a> (EEOC) filed a discrimination lawsuit against Target Corporation for unlawfully denying reasonable accommodation to an employee with multiple disability-based impairments and substantially reducing his work hours due to the medical conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> According to the claims in the EEOC press release, Target's actions violated Title I of the <a href="/wiki/Americans_With_Disabilities_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Americans With Disabilities Act">Americans With Disabilities Act</a> (ADA) and Title I of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1991" title="Civil Rights Act of 1991">Civil Rights Act of 1991</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Philanthropy" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Target is consistently ranked as one of the most <a href="/wiki/Philanthropy" title="Philanthropy">philanthropic</a> companies in the US. It ranked No. 22 in <i>Fortune</i> magazine's "World's Most Admired Companies" for 2010, largely in part to the donation efforts of the company as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> According to a November 2005 <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> article, it ranked as the highest cash-giving company in America in percentage of income given (2.1%).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Target donates around 5 percent of its pre-tax operating profit; it gives over $3 million a week (up from $2 million in years prior) to the communities in which it operates. It also gives a percentage of charges from its Target Visa to schools designated by the cardholders. To date, Target has given over $150 million to schools across the United States through this program.
</p><p>Further evidence of Target's philanthropy can be found in the Target House complex in <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis, Tennessee</a>, a long-term housing solution for families of patients at the city's <a href="/wiki/St._Jude_Children%27s_Research_Hospital" title="St. Jude Children's Research Hospital">St. Jude Children's Research Hospital</a>. The corporation led the way with more than $27 million in donations, which made available 96 fully furnished apartments for families needing to stay at St. Jude over 90 days.
</p><p>Target has a no-solicitation rule at its properties, as it seeks to provide a "distraction-free shopping experience for its guests." Exemptions to this policy were previously made for the <a href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a> red kettles and bell-ringers outside Target stores during the holidays through Christmas. In 2004, however, Target asked the organization to explore alternate methods to partner with Target. Target donates to local Salvation Army chapters through its grant program and annually to the <a href="/wiki/United_Way_of_America" title="United Way of America">United Way of America</a> (the Salvation Army is a member of the United Way coalition).
</p><p>In 2005, Target and the Salvation Army<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> created a joint effort called "The Target/Salvation Army Wish List", where online shoppers could donate goods to the organization for hurricane victims by buying them directly from Target.com between November 25, 2005, and January 25, 2006. In 2006, they created another joint effort called "The Target/Salvation Army Angel Giving Tree",<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> which is an online version of the Salvation Army's Angel Tree program;<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> in addition to donating proceeds made from the sales of limited edition Harvey Lewis angel ornaments within Target's stores. During the Thanksgiving holiday of 2006, Target and the Salvation Army partnered with magician <a href="/wiki/David_Blaine" title="David Blaine">David Blaine</a> to send several families on a shopping spree the morning of <a href="/wiki/Black_Friday_(shopping)" title="Black Friday (shopping)">Black Friday</a>. The challenge held that if Blaine could successfully work his way out of a spinning gyroscope by the morning of Black Friday, then several families would receive $500 shopping certificates. The challenge was completed successfully by Blaine.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p><p>During disasters, Target has been a major benefactor for relief efforts. Target provided monetary and product donations during the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>; it also donated money for relief efforts for the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 tsunami</a> in South Asia and donated $1.5 million (US) to the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a> in the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> in 2005. It also allowed its store properties in the affected area to be used as command centers for relief organizations and donated supplies such as water and bug spray.
</p><p>Target will often donate its unused, returned or seasonal merchandise (particularly clothing) to <a href="/wiki/Goodwill_Industries" title="Goodwill Industries">Goodwill Industries</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Environmental record" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2007, Target Corporation agreed to reduce its sales on all materials containing <a href="/wiki/Polyvinyl_chloride" title="Polyvinyl chloride">polyvinyl chloride</a> (PVC).<sup id="cite_ref-newswire1_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newswire1-80">[80]</a></sup> Testers found toxic lead and <a href="/wiki/Phthalate" title="Phthalate">phthalates</a> and large amounts of PVC in toys, lunch boxes, baby bibs, jewelry, garden hoses, mini blinds, Christmas trees, and electronics.<sup id="cite_ref-newswire1_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newswire1-80">[80]</a></sup> Several studies have shown that chemicals in vinyl chloride can cause serious health problems for children and adults.<sup id="cite_ref-newswire1_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newswire1-80">[80]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_Medical_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Illinois Medical Center">University of Illinois Medical Center</a> in Chicago states that people who use products containing PVC can become exposed with harmful toxic phthalates and lead, which eventually can become a big contributor with <a href="/wiki/Dioxins_and_dioxin-like_compounds" title="Dioxins and dioxin-like compounds">dioxins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newswire1_80-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newswire1-80">[80]</a></sup> Lois Gibbs, executive director of the Center for Health, Environment, and Justice, stated, "Target is doing the right thing by moving away from PVC and switching to safer alternatives."<sup id="cite_ref-newswire1_80-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newswire1-80">[80]</a></sup> Other companies reducing the PVC on their shelves include Walmart, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">Johnson &amp; Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>, and Apple.<sup id="cite_ref-newswire1_80-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newswire1-80">[80]</a></sup> Target stores have been taking environmental measures by reusing materials within their stores and recycling products such as broken hangers, cardboard, and rechargeable batteries.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Target is beginning to reduce energy use with energy-efficient storefronts and reducing waste with recycling programs.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> All Target stores in the United States use plastic carts with metal frames. In mid-2006, Target took it a step further when it began introducing a newer cart design made entirely of plastic. It also uses the same design in its hand-use baskets.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p><p>Target released a 13-page report in 2007 that outlined their current and future plans for becoming more earth-friendly according to <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a>. Such efforts include installing sand filtration systems for the stores' wastewater. Recycling programs will be aimed at garment hangers, corrugated cardboard, electronics, shopping carts, shrink wrap, construction wastes, carpeting, and ceiling tiles and roofing materials. All stores in <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> will be partnered with <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Gas_%26_Electric" title="Oklahoma Gas &amp; Electric">Oklahoma Gas &amp; Electric</a> to exclusively use <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a> for all Target stores in order to reduce <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions. Stores nationwide use only <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">LED</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fluorescent_lamp" title="Fluorescent lamp">fluorescent lights</a> and low-flow restrooms that reduce wastewater by 30%. Some Target stores are installing roof gardens or <a href="/wiki/Green_roof" title="Green roof">green roofs</a>, which absorb stormwater and cut down on <a href="/wiki/Surface_runoff" title="Surface runoff">surface runoff</a>, mitigate temperature fluctuations and provide habitats for birds. There are currently four green-roof Target stores in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>.
</p><p>Target carries over 700 organic and alternative products from brands such as <a href="/wiki/Archer_Farms" class="mw-redirect" title="Archer Farms">Archer Farms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burt%27s_Bees" title="Burt's Bees">Burt's Bees</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Method_Products" class="mw-redirect" title="Method Products">Method Products</a>. They also sell clothes made from organic cotton, non-toxic cleaners, low-energy lighting and electronics, non-toxic and non-animal tested cosmetics, and furniture made from recycled materials. As of June 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Target has been offering <a href="/wiki/Reusable_shopping_bag" title="Reusable shopping bag">reusable shopping bags</a> as an alternative to disposable plastic bags. Target gift cards are made from corn-based resins. All of the stores' packaging is done with a modified paperboard/clamshell option and has goals for phasing out <a href="/wiki/Plastic_wrap" title="Plastic wrap">plastic wrap</a> completely.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p><p>In collaboration with <a href="/wiki/MBH_Architects" title="MBH Architects">MBH Architects</a>, Target's first "green" building was a 100,000+ square foot Target store built-in 1995 in <a href="/wiki/Fullerton,_California" title="Fullerton, California">Fullerton, California</a>. It was a part of the EPA Energy Star Showcase for its use of <a href="/wiki/Skylight" title="Skylight">skylights</a> that cut the original energy consumption by 24% with a 5-year payback.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Target and MBH Architects were awarded the "Green Lights Partner/Ally of the Year Award".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p>Target is the only national retailer employing a Garment Hanger reuse program, which keeps millions of pounds of metal and plastic out of <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfills</a>. In 2007, this program prevented 434 million hangers from entering landfills.
</p><p>On June 15, 2009, the California Attorney General and 20 California District Attorneys filed a lawsuit in <a href="/wiki/Alameda_County,_California" title="Alameda County, California">Alameda County</a> alleging that Target stores across the state have been illegally dumping <a href="/wiki/Hazardous_waste" title="Hazardous waste">hazardous wastes</a> in landfills.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p><p>On October 1, 2009, Target Corporation agreed to pay a $600,000 civil penalty for importing and selling a variety of toys with <a href="/wiki/Lead_paint" title="Lead paint">lead paint</a> levels that were higher than is legally allowed. The <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Products_Safety_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumer Products Safety Commission">Consumer Products Safety Commission</a> alleged that "Target knowingly imported and sold the illegal Chinese-made toys between May 2006 and August 2007."<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> A similar problem occurred a few months later in February 2010, when Target pulled <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine's Day">Valentine's Day</a> "message bears" from its shelves at the request of the California attorney general's office. The bears, which were manufactured in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, contained more lead than is permissible under federal law for children under 12.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Class_action" title="Class action">class action</a> suit was filed in 2014 in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. District Court for the Northern District of Ohio">U.S. District Court for the Northern District of Ohio</a>, on behalf of consumers in Ohio that purchased Target-brand <a href="/wiki/Wet_wipes" class="mw-redirect" title="Wet wipes">wet wipes</a>. The lawsuit filed against Target Corporation alleges the retailer misled consumers by marking the packaging on its up &amp; up® brand wipes as flushable and safe for sewer and septic systems. The lawsuit also alleges that so-called flushable wipes are a public health hazard because they are alleged to clog pumps at municipal waste-treatment facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p><p>On Dec. 5, 2018, Alameda County District Attorney O’Malley announced fining Target $7.4 million for putting illegal e-waste, medical supplies and private information into the garbage.<sup id="cite_ref-ACDAO-121418_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACDAO-121418-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Customer_privacy">Customer privacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Customer privacy" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In December 2013, a <a href="/wiki/Data_breach" title="Data breach">data breach</a> of Target's systems affected up to 110 million customers.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Compromised customer information included names, phone numbers, email and mailing addresses.<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo_millions_more_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo_millions_more-94">[94]</a></sup> In March 2015, Target reached a class-action settlement with affected consumers for $10 million (plus class-action attorney fees).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> In May 2016, Target settled with affected banks and credit unions for $39 million (plus class-action attorney fees), of which $19 million would be disbursed by a <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a> program.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_relations">Labor relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Labor relations" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>In 2015, Target followed <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> in raising the minimum wage to $9 per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Two years later, Target announced that the minimum hourly wage would be increased to $11 by October 2017 and pledged to raise it to $15 (referred to as "living wage" by labor advocates) by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> By April 2019, the company announced that it was on track to meet this goal, increasing its minimum wage to $13 per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_identity">Corporate identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Corporate identity" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Logo" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional"><li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
