</ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Differentiation_from_competitors">Differentiation from competitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Differentiation from competitors" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Since its founding, it has intended to differentiate its stores from its competitors by offering what it believes is more upscale, trend-forward merchandise at lower costs, rather than the traditional concept of focusing on low-priced goods. Douglas J. Dayton, one of the Dayton brothers, explained John Geisse's concept:
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;"><tbody><tr><td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">"We will offer high-quality merchandise at low margins because we are cutting expenses. We would much rather do this than trumpet dramatic price cuts on cheap merchandise."<sup id="cite_ref-growth_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-growth-49">[49]</a></sup></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr></tbody></table><p>As a result, Target stores tend to attract younger customers than Walmart, among other competitors. The <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> Target shopper is 40, the youngest of all major discount retailers that Target competes directly against. The median household income of Target's customer base is roughly $64,000. Roughly 76% of Target customers are female, and more than 43% have children at home. About 80% have attended college and 57% have completed college.<sup id="cite_ref-community_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-community-101">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-factcard_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factcard-102">[102]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2008, Target announced plans to fight the perception that their products are more expensive than those of other discount retailers. It added perishables to their inventory, cut back on discretionary items, and spent three-quarters of their marketing budget on advertising that emphasizes value and includes actual prices of items featured in ads. Target also planned to slow its expansion from about 100 stores a year down to 70 stores a year.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p><p>Target stores are designed to be more attractive than large <a href="/wiki/Big-box_store" title="Big-box store">big-box stores</a> by having wider aisles drop ceilings, a more attractive presentation of merchandise, and generally cleaner fixtures. Special attention is given to the design of the store environment: graphics reinforce its advertising imagery, while shelves are dressed with contemporary signage, backdrops, and liners, often printed on inexpensive material such as paper, corrugated and foam boards. Some stores, particularly those in the vicinity of major airports, have a <a href="/wiki/Bullseye_(target)" title="Bullseye (target)">bullseye</a> painted on the roof that can be seen from above: the stores in <a href="/wiki/East_Point,_Georgia" title="East Point, Georgia">East Point, Georgia</a> near <a href="/wiki/Hartsfield-Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Hartsfield-Jackson Atlanta International Airport">Hartsfield-Jackson Atlanta International Airport</a>; <a href="/wiki/Rosemont,_Illinois" title="Rosemont, Illinois">Rosemont, Illinois</a>, near <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O'Hare International Airport">O'Hare International Airport</a>; <a href="/wiki/Potomac_Yard" title="Potomac Yard">Potomac Yard, Virginia</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Washington_National_Airport" title="Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport">Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport</a>; <a href="/wiki/College_Point,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="College Point, New York">College Point, New York</a> (Queens), east of <a href="/wiki/LaGuardia_Airport" title="LaGuardia Airport">LaGuardia Airport</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Richfield,_Minnesota" title="Richfield, Minnesota">Richfield, Minnesota</a>, adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis%E2%80%93St._Paul_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis–St. Paul International Airport">Minneapolis–St. Paul International Airport</a> are among such locations.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p><p>Target stores do not sell <a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">firearms</a>. In the early 1990s, they ceased sales of <a href="/wiki/Toy_gun" title="Toy gun">toy guns</a> that looked realistic and limited its toy gun selection to ones that were brightly colored and oddly shaped. In 2014, Target also "respectfully" asked their guests to leave any firearms at home when visiting the store.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> They do not sell tobacco products and have not sold cigarettes since 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-responsibility_report_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-responsibility_report-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p><p>Most Target stores don't play music, but may be changing that from 2017 with a rebranding process, adding music to the rebranded stores.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Targ.C3.A9t"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Targét">Targét</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Targét" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Some people jokingly give Target the pseudo-French pronunciation <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ʒ/: 's' in 'pleasure'">ʒ</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">tar-<span style="font-size:90%">ZHAY</span></i></a>, as though it were an upscale boutique. Though this practice is often attributed to <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah Winfrey</a>'s usage on <a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">her television show</a>, it is first attested in 1962, the year the first Target store opened. Target once sold a line of shoes called "Miss Targé";<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> this was reinforced by a 1980s television advertisement starring <a href="/wiki/Didi_Conn" title="Didi Conn">Didi Conn</a>. This pronunciation has also led some people to incorrectly believe that the company is French-owned.<sup id="cite_ref-rowley_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowley-48">[48]</a></sup> In recognition of the nickname's popularity and cachet, Target Corporation licensed its new name and logo to Brand Central LLC in 2006, complete with an accent over the letter "E" for a new line of clothing aimed at more upscale fashion customers. The line, "Targét Couture", was originally sold in Los Angeles-based store Intuition, which deals with high-end brands.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Washington_Post_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Washington_Post-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Celebutopia_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Celebutopia-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Nomenclature">Nomenclature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Nomenclature" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Target uses a practice that was derived in 1989 from <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a><sup id="cite_ref-rowley_48-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rowley-48">[48]</a></sup> by calling its customers "Guests", its employees "Team Members", and its supervisors "Team Leaders". Also, managers are known as "Executive Team Leaders (ETLs)," "Senior Team Leaders (SRTLs)," or "Guest Service Team Leaders (GSTLs)" and the Store Manager is known as the "Store Team Leader (STL)". Further up the "chain of command" are "District Team Leaders (DTL)", "Group Team Leaders (GTL) (sometimes also Group Vice President)", Regional Team Leaders (RTL) (sometimes also Regional Vice President), and finally corporate-level executives.
</p><p>This practice began to be revised in 2018 and became more widespread in 2019 as the Group Team Leader became the Group Operations Director. District Team Leader became the District Senior Director. The Store Team Leader became Store Director. Executive Team Leaders were shortened to Executive Team Lead. Other Team Leaders retained their title though some of the department names changed such as Guest Service Team Leader was renamed Service &amp; Engagement Team Leader. Front of store team members was renamed Guest Advocates. Specialty areas in Style, Beauty and Tech are considered Consultants. Other areas such as General Merchandise, Presentation, Inbound, Fulfillment, Food Service and Reverse Logistics are considered Experts.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Product_lines_and_partnerships">Product lines and partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Product lines and partnerships" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Target has many exclusive deals with various designers and name brands, including Finnish design company <a href="/wiki/Marimekko" title="Marimekko">Marimekko</a>; architect <a href="/wiki/Michael_Graves" title="Michael Graves">Michael Graves</a>; athletic wear company <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a>; Portland-based undergarment designer <a href="/wiki/Pair_of_Thieves" title="Pair of Thieves">Pair of Thieves</a>; Italian fashion label <a href="/wiki/Fiorucci" title="Fiorucci">Fiorucci</a>; fashion designers <a href="/wiki/Lilly_Pulitzer" title="Lilly Pulitzer">Lilly Pulitzer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liz_Lange" title="Liz Lange">Liz Lange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mossimo" title="Mossimo">Mossimo Giannulli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Mizrahi" title="Isaac Mizrahi">Isaac Mizrahi</a>, among others. To further increase their fashion profile, Target also created its fashion-forward <a href="/wiki/Go_International" title="Go International">Go International</a> line, which hires famous designers to design collections available only for a few months.<sup id="cite_ref-michael_graves_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-michael_graves-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>Target, after hiring architect Michael Graves to design the scaffolding used to renovate the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Monument" title="Washington Monument">Washington Monument</a> and contributing US$6 million to the restoration plan, introduced its first designer line of products in 1999, the Michael Graves Collection of housewares and home decor products.<sup id="cite_ref-michael_graves_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-michael_graves-113">[113]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a> have followed Target's lead by signing exclusive designers to their stores as well. Target also partners with well-established national brands to create exclusive collections for its stores.<sup id="cite_ref-michael_graves_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-michael_graves-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>Target also signed an exclusive deal with <a href="/wiki/Food_Network" title="Food Network">Food Network</a> to sell VHS tapes of TV shows featuring popular chefs such as <a href="/wiki/Alton_Brown" title="Alton Brown">Alton Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paula_Deen" title="Paula Deen">Paula Deen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rachael_Ray" title="Rachael Ray">Rachael Ray</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 2005, Target introduced a major revision of <a href="/wiki/Prescription_drug" title="Prescription drug">prescription</a> bottles, which it calls the <a href="/wiki/ClearRx" title="ClearRx">ClearRx</a> system. The redesigned bottles are color-coded, flattened-out and turned upside down, providing more room for the label. This system was based on the patent<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> by student Deborah Adler and was named one of <i>TIME's</i> "Most Amazing Inventions of 2005".<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p><p>Sometimes manufacturers will create red-colored items exclusively for Target.  In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> produced a red <a href="/wiki/List_of_Game_Boy_colors_and_styles#Special_Edition_Variants_5" title="List of Game Boy colors and styles">special edition variant</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a>, which featured the Target logo above the screen.<sup id="cite_ref-gameboyadvance_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gameboyadvance-116">[116]</a></sup></p><p>In 2005, <a href="/wiki/IFC_(U.S._TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="IFC (U.S. TV network)">IFC</a> began a partnership with Target to promote a selection of independent films, both in Target stores and on IFC Monday nights at 9:00 pm Eastern. Originally titled <i>IFC Cinema Red</i>, the promotion was rebranded on-air as <i>The Spotlight</i> in 2007. The in-store headers refer to the selected titles as <i>IFC Indies – Independent films chosen for Target by the Independent Film Channel.</i><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p><p>In 2016, Target began to enforce <a href="/wiki/Gender_neutrality" title="Gender neutrality">gender neutrality</a> in its marketing of toys, and no longer explicitly listed specific toys as being for "boys" or "girls". This practice was expanded with the February 2016 launch of new children's decor line, Pillowfort, which will replace its Circo brand and feature more gender-neutral designs and color schemes.<sup id="cite_ref-startrib-pillowfort_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-startrib-pillowfort-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Gift_cards">Gift cards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Gift cards" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Target GiftCard is the retailing division's <a href="/wiki/Stored-value_card" title="Stored-value card">stored-value card</a> or <a href="/wiki/Gift_card" title="Gift card">gift card</a>. Target sells more gift cards than any other retailer in the United States and is one of the top sellers, by dollars and units, in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The unique designs of their cards contribute to their higher sales, as well as Target's policy of no expiration dates or service fees.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Past and current designs include <a href="/wiki/Lenticular_printing" title="Lenticular printing">lenticular</a>, "scratch and sniff" (such as peppermint during the Christmas season), <a href="/wiki/Phosphorescence" title="Phosphorescence">glow in the dark</a>, <a href="/wiki/LED" class="mw-redirect" title="LED">LED</a> light-up, a gift card on the side of a <a href="/wiki/Soap_bubble" title="Soap bubble">bubble blower</a>, a gift card that can function as a <a href="/wiki/CD-ROM" title="CD-ROM">CD-ROM</a>, and even a gift card that allows the sender to record a voice message. A current environmentally friendly gift card is made from <a href="/wiki/Bioplastic" title="Bioplastic">bioplastic</a> manufactured from corn.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Target rolled out a new <a href="/wiki/MP3_player" title="MP3 player">MP3 player</a> gift card for the 2006 holiday season. It holds 12 songs and must be purchased with an initial value of at least $50.
</p><p>Beginning in January 2010, Target Stores rolled out Mobile GiftCards, through which one can produce a GiftCard barcode on any web-capable cell phone. This data matrix barcode can be scanned at a Target POS like any physical card barcode, and balances can be stored, retrieved, and gifted with the convenience of a cell phone.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>Some of these unique design ideas are patented, and these patents are assigned to the Target Brands subsidiary. For example, some such Target GiftCard designs feature a wooden front side. On May 24, 2005, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a> granted U.S. patent D505,450 for the "ornamental design for credit or stored value card with wood layer" to inventors Amy L. Lauer and John D. Mayhew.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> U.S. patent 7004398, for the "stored-value card assembly including a stored-value card, an edible product, and a wrapper", was granted to Michael R. Francis and Barry C. Brooks on February 28, 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Both patents have been assigned by their inventors to Target Brands, Inc.
</p><p>Target GiftCards are also collector's items. Some of the first gift cards issued are valued at over $300 (even though the card doesn't have any money on it). Every year, Target introduces new Holiday GiftCards. In 2007, Target's Holiday GiftCards featured a wind-up flashlight, a musical gift card, a gift card that lights up, and a scented gift card.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Target_forensic_services">Target forensic services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Target forensic services" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>In 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> revealed that Target is operating two criminal <a href="/wiki/Forensics" class="mw-redirect" title="Forensics">forensics</a> laboratories, one at its headquarters and the other in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Originally, the lab was created with the role of investigating internal instances of theft, fraud, and other criminal actions that have occurred on its own properties. Eventually, the company began offering <a href="/wiki/Pro_bono" title="Pro bono">pro bono</a> services to law enforcement agencies across the country. Target's Forensic Services has assisted agencies at all levels of government, including such federal agencies as the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Alcohol,_Tobacco,_Firearms_and_Explosives" title="Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives">Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secret_Service" title="United States Secret Service">United States Secret Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-police_work_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-police_work-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_and_controversy">Criticism and controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Criticism and controversy" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_welfare_concerns">Animal welfare concerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Animal welfare concerns" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Mercy_for_Animals" title="Mercy for Animals">Mercy for Animals</a>, a non-profit organization dedicated to preventing cruelty to farmed animals and promoting compassionate food choices and policies, uncovered alleged <a href="/wiki/Animal_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Animal abuse">animal abuse</a> at a Target egg supplier, Sparboe Farms.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p><p>The investigation received international media attention; it aired first on ABC's <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/World_News_Tonight_with_Diane_Sawyer" class="mw-redirect" title="World News Tonight with Diane Sawyer">World News Tonight with Diane Sawyer</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/20/20_(American_TV_program)" title="20/20 (American TV program)">20/20</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> As a result of the investigation and the public outcry that followed, Target immediately discontinued its relationship with the company.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In January 2016, Target Corp. announced that it will discontinue the use of eggs from caged hens, and become entirely cage-free by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Sun-Times:_Target_stores_switching_to_cage-free_eggs_by_2025_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Sun-Times:_Target_stores_switching_to_cage-free_eggs_by_2025-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Refusal_to_stock_albums_after_digital_release">Refusal to stock albums after digital release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Refusal to stock albums after digital release" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Target initially refused to sell <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ocean" title="Frank Ocean">Frank Ocean</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Channel_Orange" title="Channel Orange">Channel Orange</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">self-titled album</a>, due to those records becoming available to <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital retailers</a>, like <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes</a>, before physical copies were made. Target representatives argued that doing so impacted how well those records would sell at Target stores, and stocking them could cause the corporation to lose money.<sup id="cite_ref-newsfeed.time.com_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsfeed.time.com-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBTQ">LGBTQ</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: LGBTQ" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> was expected to give the store an exclusive expanded edition of her then upcoming album <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(album)" title="Born This Way (album)">Born This Way</a></i>, but ended the deal after discovering that the then CEO Gregg Steinhafel donated to a political action group that supported an anti-gay candidate.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Target apologized<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> and began its outward support of the  <a href="/wiki/LGBTQ" class="mw-redirect" title="LGBTQ">LGBTQ</a> community. In 2012 it began by stocking <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">gay pride</a> merchandise and donating half of the profits to <a href="/wiki/GLSEN" title="GLSEN">GLSEN</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2014 it began featuring LGBTQ individuals and couples in national advertising.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In 2015, Target debuted their #takepride campaign, and partnered with GLSEN to produce a mini-documentary celebrating their 25th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Target sponsors many LGBTQ non-profits including <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Campaign" title="Human Rights Campaign">Human Rights Campaign</a>, <a href="/wiki/GLSEN" title="GLSEN">GLSEN</a>, <a href="/wiki/GLAAD" title="GLAAD">GLAAD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Family_Equality_Council" title="Family Equality Council">Family Equality Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/NGLCC" class="mw-redirect" title="NGLCC">NGLCC</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Williams_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Williams Institute">Williams Institute</a>. For the last three years, Target has been the presenting sponsor of GLAAD's <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Day" title="Spirit Day">Spirit Day</a>. In 2017, Target was the founding partner of New York City's Pride Youth. Target has been ranked by LGBTQ Consumers as a favorite brand in 2016 &amp; 2017 by Community Marketing Inc's 10th &amp; 11th Annual LGBT Community Survey. Target has a score of 100 on the Human Rights Campaign Corporate Equality Index<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> for their corporate policies and practices pertinent to lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender and queer employees. In 2019, Target donated $100,000 to GLSEN.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Store_closures">Store closures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Store closures" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On Wednesday, November 4, 2015, Target announced that it would be closing thirteen of its stores in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In a statement, Target spokesperson Kristy Welker said, "The decision to close a Target store is not made lightly. We typically decide to close a store after careful consideration of the long-term financial performance of a particular location."<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The community of <a href="/wiki/New_Ulm,_Minnesota" title="New Ulm, Minnesota">New Ulm, Minnesota</a> protested the closure of the store in town with a social media group entitled "Save New Ulm Target", which gained 10,000 members within a week of its creation.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Despite the efforts of many members of the community and even Mayor Robert Buessman of New Ulm, Target upheld its decision to close the New Ulm store.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The New Ulm store and the other twelve stores closed on January 30, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id=".22Bathroom_policy.22_and_boycott"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='"Bathroom_policy"_and_boycott'>"Bathroom policy" and boycott</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title='Edit section: "Bathroom policy" and boycott' data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TargetRestroom.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/TargetRestroom.jpg/220px-TargetRestroom.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/TargetRestroom.jpg/220px-TargetRestroom.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TargetRestroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Restroom at a Target store.</div></div></div>
<p>In April 2016, Target announced on its website that it would allow transgender customers and employees access to use restrooms and changing areas that correspond with the gender with which they identify, except where local laws require otherwise. The announcement read: "We believe that everyone—every team member, every guest, and every community—deserves to be protected from discrimination, and treated equally. Consistent with this belief, Target supports the federal Equality Act, which provides protections to LGBT individuals, and opposes action that enables discrimination. In our stores, we demonstrate our commitment to an inclusive experience in many ways. Most relevant for the conversations currently underway, we welcome transgender team members and guests to use the restroom or fitting room facility that corresponds with their gender identity."<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i> called this "the most prominent position taken by a national retailer".<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> In response, the <a href="/wiki/American_Family_Association" title="American Family Association">American Family Association</a> (AFA) launched a nationwide boycott; by April 28 about one million people had signed the AFA's petition.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Around the time of publicity about the policy, polls reported a drop from 42% to 38% of consumers noting they would shop at Target.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> In mid-May, CEO Cornell said the boycott impacted "just a handful of stores across the country".<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Some observers, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortune Magazine">Fortune</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Phil Wahba, believed that Target's bathroom policy may have caused part of Target's drop in shopper traffic during the <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year#United_States" title="Fiscal year">second quarter</a> of 2016. On August 17, Target announced it would add a third, private, single-stall locking bathroom at many of its stores.<sup id="cite_ref-fortune-20mil_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune-20mil-156">[156]</a></sup> In 2017, Cornell claimed not to know about, or have approved, the policy before it was published. The policy cost the business US$20 million and caused sales to fall nearly 6% in the three quarters following.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fortune-20mil_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune-20mil-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Absence_of_AEDs_in_stores">Absence of AEDs in stores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Absence of AEDs in stores" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, the California Supreme Court ruled that Target stores do not have a positive duty to keep AEDs (Automated External Defibrillators) in stores for purposes of first aid. This decision came after a 49-year-old woman died following a heart attack in a Target store, and two family members filed a wrongful death lawsuit.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_sponsorships">Major sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Major sponsorships" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_IndyCar.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Target_IndyCar.jpg/220px-Target_IndyCar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="944" data-file-height="705"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 164px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Target_IndyCar.jpg/220px-Target_IndyCar.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="164" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Target_IndyCar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Target Chip Ganassi Racing IndyCar visiting <a href="/wiki/Purdue_University" title="Purdue University">Purdue University</a></div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Events" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul><li>Target often supports major awards shows, such as the <a href="/wiki/Emmys" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmys">Emmys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globes" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globes">Golden Globes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammys" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammys">Grammys</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Oscars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></li>
<li>Target Corporation is a major sponsor of the annual <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis_Aquatennial" title="Minneapolis Aquatennial">Minneapolis Aquatennial</a>, where it hosts the Target Fireworks Show, the largest annual fireworks show west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> and the fourth largest annual fireworks show in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></li>
<li>Target was a sponsor of the 2006–2007 New Year's <a href="/wiki/Times_Square_Ball" title="Times Square Ball">Times Square Ball</a> Drop and had its logo placed on the confetti dropped during the celebrations as well as specially designed "2007" glasses.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sports" data-section="39" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Minnesota_United_FC">Minnesota United FC</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Minnesota United FC" data-section="40" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerome_Theisson_PHI_vs_MIN_2017-09-09_(36975333956).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Jerome_Theisson_PHI_vs_MIN_2017-09-09_%2836975333956%29.jpg/240px-Jerome_Theisson_PHI_vs_MIN_2017-09-09_%2836975333956%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="160" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 240px;height: 160px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Jerome_Theisson_PHI_vs_MIN_2017-09-09_%2836975333956%29.jpg/240px-Jerome_Theisson_PHI_vs_MIN_2017-09-09_%2836975333956%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="240" data-height="160" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jerome_Theisson_PHI_vs_MIN_2017-09-09_(36975333956).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Minnesota_United_FC" title="Minnesota United FC">Minnesota United FC</a> player with Target's logo on the jersey as well as on the stadium's advertisement boards.</div></div></div>
<p>In January 2017, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_United_FC" title="Minnesota United FC">Minnesota United FC</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> expansion team debuting for the 2017 Season, announced that Target would be the team's front-of-jersey match kit sponsor, as well as sponsoring MLS overall. This brings one of the largest sponsors in the league, especially for an expansion team making its debut appearance. The team also has an advantage of having a large, well-known hometown brand versus an entity outside the region, in addition to the financial benefits of such a large sponsor.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_League_Soccer_and_US_Youth_Soccer"><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> and US Youth Soccer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Major League Soccer and US Youth Soccer" data-section="41" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In 2017, Target announced a series of national, local and charitable initiatives that mark the retailer's largest-ever push into team sports. Target became an Official Partner of Major League Soccer in a multi-year deal that includes airtime during MLS broadcasts on Univision, FOX Sports and ESPN, opportunities for in-stadium experiences, player appearances and ownership of certain major MLS platform.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Target also announced a $14 million commitment to local youth soccer through two new national initiatives—an $8 million local soccer grant program, and a $6 million partnership with the U.S. Soccer Foundation to build 100 new soccer play spaces by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Target is the official sponsor of 2017<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup>&amp; 2018<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> MLS All Star Games.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_Sports">Extreme Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Extreme Sports" data-section="42" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Target sponsors pro <a href="/wiki/Freestyle_motocross" title="Freestyle motocross">freestyle motocross</a> rider <a href="/wiki/Nate_Adams" title="Nate Adams">Nate Adams</a>, pro snowboarder/skateboarder <a href="/wiki/Shaun_White" title="Shaun White">Shaun White</a>, pro skateboarder <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodriguez_(skateboarder)" title="Paul Rodriguez (skateboarder)">Paul Rodriguez</a>, pro BMX rider <a href="/wiki/Mat_Hoffman" title="Mat Hoffman">Mat Hoffman</a> and pro surfer <a href="/wiki/Kolohe_Andino" title="Kolohe Andino">Kolohe Andino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Chip_Ganassi_Racing">Chip Ganassi Racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Chip Ganassi Racing" data-section="43" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kyle_Larson_-_Chevrolet_-_2017.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Kyle_Larson_-_Chevrolet_-_2017.jpg/220px-Kyle_Larson_-_Chevrolet_-_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="608" data-file-height="356"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 129px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Kyle_Larson_-_Chevrolet_-_2017.jpg/220px-Kyle_Larson_-_Chevrolet_-_2017.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="129" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kyle_Larson_-_Chevrolet_-_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Target car driven by Chip Ganassi Racing driver Kyle Larson in the Monster Energy NASCAR Cup Series in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Target was a long-time sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/IndyCar" title="IndyCar">IndyCar</a> and <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> racing teams of <a href="/wiki/Chip_Ganassi_Racing" title="Chip Ganassi Racing">Chip Ganassi Racing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nbc_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbc-171">[171]</a></sup> Target's relationship with Ganassi in IndyCar go back to 1990 when it began sponsoring <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Cheever" title="Eddie Cheever">Eddie Cheever</a>. Some of their most famous drivers in the 1990s include <a href="/wiki/Michael_Andretti" title="Michael Andretti">Michael Andretti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Herta" title="Bryan Herta">Bryan Herta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arie_Luyendyk" title="Arie Luyendyk">Arie Luyendyk</a>. In the late 1990s, Target Chip Ganassi Racing had a four-year run of winning championships in <a href="/wiki/Champ_Car" class="mw-redirect" title="Champ Car">CART</a>, winning 1996 with <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Vasser" title="Jimmy Vasser">Jimmy Vasser</a>, 1997 and 1998 with <a href="/wiki/Alex_Zanardi" title="Alex Zanardi">Alex Zanardi</a>, and 1999 with <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Montoya" title="Juan Pablo Montoya">Juan Pablo Montoya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Ganassi won their first <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_500" title="Indianapolis 500">Indianapolis 500</a> in 2000. The team moved full-time into the rival <a href="/wiki/Indy_Racing_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Indy Racing League">Indy Racing League</a> in 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> and won in its first year of full-time competition, with <a href="/wiki/Scott_Dixon" title="Scott Dixon">Scott Dixon</a>. Dixon won the championship again in 2008. The 2009 season marked the 20th anniversary of the Target race program. Franchitti won his second career IndyCar championship, and with Scott Dixon finishing second, gave Target a one-two sweep in the IndyCar Series. Dixon and Franchitti won 10 of 17 races (Dixon-5, Franchitti-5) and tied the team record from 1998 where Alex Zanardi and Jimmy Vasser combined to win 10 in the 19-race 1998 CART season. In 2010, Franchitti won the Indianapolis 500. He also won the series championship for the Target team, by five points over second-place finisher <a href="/wiki/Will_Power" title="Will Power">Will Power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p><p>Target started sponsoring stock cars in 2001 with <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Marlin" title="Sterling Marlin">Sterling Marlin</a> when Chip Ganassi bought into the <a href="/wiki/Felix_Sabates" title="Felix Sabates">Felix Sabates</a> stock car team.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2002_NASCAR_Winston_Cup_Series" title="2002 NASCAR Winston Cup Series">2002 NASCAR Winston Cup Series</a> season, the No. 41 Chip Ganassi Target car was driven by <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Spencer" title="Jimmy Spencer">Jimmy Spencer</a>, and from 2003 to 2005, <a href="/wiki/Casey_Mears" title="Casey Mears">Casey Mears</a> drove the car. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Reed_Sorenson" title="Reed Sorenson">Reed Sorenson</a> took over the No. 41 when Mears moved to a different Chip Ganassi car on the same team. Sorenson drove the car through the 2008 season, and Target has also had some major sponsorship time on the Ganassi Racing No. 40 car with <a href="/wiki/Dario_Franchitti" title="Dario Franchitti">Dario Franchitti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Mayfield" title="Jeremy Mayfield">Jeremy Mayfield</a> who subbed for the injured Franchitti. The 40 team has since been shut down. For 2009, the Target sponsorship moved to the No. 42 driven by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Montoya" title="Juan Pablo Montoya">Juan Pablo Montoya</a> with the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Earnhardt_Ganassi_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Earnhardt Ganassi Racing">Earnhardt Ganassi Racing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Target also sponsored Earnhardt Ganassi Racing's No. 8 car driven by <a href="/wiki/Aric_Almirola" title="Aric Almirola">Aric Almirola</a>, which it co-sponsors in some races with other sponsors such as <a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero" title="Guitar Hero">Guitar Hero</a> and <a href="/wiki/TomTom" title="TomTom">TomTom</a> until the team was disbanded in May 2009. <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Larson" title="Kyle Larson">Kyle Larson</a> took over the No. 42 in 2014 and Target sponsored the No. 51 of <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Racing_(NASCAR_team)" title="Phoenix Racing (NASCAR team)">Phoenix Racing</a> for Larson's <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Cup_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Sprint Cup Series">Sprint Cup Series</a> debut.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>

href="/wiki/Target_Field" title="Target Field">Target Field</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The Target Chip Ganassi<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> car driven by Dario Franchitti won the <a href="/wiki/2010_Indianapolis_500" title="2010 Indianapolis 500">94th running</a> of the Indianapolis 500 on Sunday, May 30, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-INDY1_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INDY1-178">[178]</a></sup></p><p>Target ended its association with IndyCar racing at the end of the 2016 season.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> In July 2017 Target announced that it would end its sponsorship of Ganassi's NASCAR team at the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-nbc_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbc-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming_rights">Naming rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Naming rights" data-section="44" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Target owns the naming rights to the <a href="/wiki/Target_Center" title="Target Center">Target Center</a> since it first opened in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Target also owns the naming rights to <a href="/wiki/Target_Field" title="Target Field">Target Field</a>, a ballpark, in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Radio" data-section="45" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Target was the founding sponsor of the <i><a href="/wiki/Weekend_America" title="Weekend America">Weekend America</a></i> radio program.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: In popular culture" data-section="46" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">
<ul><li>One of the earliest references to Target in popular culture is the film <i><a href="/wiki/Career_Opportunities_(film)" title="Career Opportunities (film)">Career Opportunities</a></i> (1991), written by <a href="/wiki/John_Hughes_(filmmaker)" title="John Hughes (filmmaker)">John Hughes</a>, in which an employee and a customer fall in love after hours inside a Target store.<sup id="cite_ref-afi_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afi-182">[182]</a></sup></li>
<li>American television program <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> featured a recurring sketch in the 2000s starring the <a href="/wiki/Target_Lady" class="mw-redirect" title="Target Lady">Target Lady</a>, an overly enthusiastic Target cashier, played by cast member <a href="/wiki/Kristen_Wiig" title="Kristen Wiig">Kristen Wiig</a>.</li>
<li>Target is the namesake of an episode of the <a href="/wiki/Superstore_(season_3)" title="Superstore (season 3)">third season</a> of American TV comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Superstore_(TV_series)" title="Superstore (TV series)">Superstore</a></i>. In the episode, an employee at big-box retailer "Cloud 9" leaves for a job at Target, and is accused of poaching employees.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(13)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="47" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-13 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-13">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Design_For_All_(product_line)" title="Design For All (product line)">Design For All (product line)</a></li></ul>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(14)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: References" data-section="48" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-14 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-14">
